## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv/dt depends on position x (restoring force), velocity v (damping), and time t (possible external driving). The equation of motion generalizes the simple harmonic oscillator with nonlinear restoring forces, damping, and/or periodic forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced nonlinear oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity-dependent dissipation)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent frequency)
- General polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (mixed polynomial)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (sinusoidal forcing with phase)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillation symmetry
- Even-power restoring forces (x²) → asymmetric potential breaking oscillation symmetry
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v → energy dissipation or injection (damping/anti-damping)
- Terms like (1 - x²)*v → amplitude-dependent damping creating limit cycles (self-sustained oscillations)
- Periodic functions of t (sin, cos) → external driving forces leading to resonance or chaos
- Product terms x*v → coupling between position and velocity indicating phase-space-dependent forces
- Cubic position terms with opposite sign to linear term → Duffing-type hardening/softening spring behavior
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system with conserved or dissipated energy
- Multiple frequency terms in t → quasi-periodic or chaotic forcing scenarios
- Position-velocity cross terms like x²*v → nonlinear damping that depends on displacement amplitude

GT: -beta*sin(v) - omega0**c0*(gamma*t + c1)*x - omega0**c2*x**c3
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-2.5126990598325*x**3 - 2.5126990598325*x*(0.0921849151045819*t + 1) - 0.774919680656294*sin(v)`

Let me expand this:
- `-2.5126990598325*x**3` (cubic in x)
- `-2.5126990598325*x - 2.5126990598325*0.0921849151045819*x*t` = `-2.5126990598325*x - 0.231588*x*t` (linear in x, and x*t term)
- `-0.774919680656294*sin(v)` (sine of v)

So the GT has terms: `x`, `x**3`, `x*t`, and `sin(v)`.

Now, the key challenge: the GT contains `sin(v)` and `x*t`. None of the candidates explicitly have `sin(v)` or `x*t` terms. Let me check what the candidates offer:

Most candidates have terms like:
- `x`, `x**3`, `v`, `v**3`, `x*cos(c*t)`, `v**2*x`, `v*x**2`, and various others.

**The `sin(v)` term:** The Taylor expansion of `sin(v) = v - v**3/6 + v**5/120 - ...`. So `sin(v)` cannot be exactly represented by a finite polynomial in `v`. None of the candidates contain `sin(v)`.

Can any combination of `v`, `v**3`, `v**5` terms match `sin(v)`? No — `sin(v)` is transcendental and cannot equal any finite polynomial in `v` for all values of `v`.

**The `x*t` term:** The GT has a term `-0.231588*x*t`. Looking at candidates, many have `x*cos(c5*t)`. Can `x*cos(c5*t)` produce `x*t`? No — `cos(c5*t)` cannot equal a linear function of `t` for all `t`. Setting `c5=0` gives `x*cos(0) = x`, which is just a constant times `x`, not `x*t`.

Some candidates have `v*cos(c*t)` terms (e.g., candidate 12, 38, 46). Could `v*cos(c*t)` somehow help? No, this gives a `v` term modulated by cosine, not `x*t`.

**Critical check:** Is there any way to get both `sin(v)` and `x*t` from the available terms? 

For `sin(v)`: No finite polynomial in `v` equals `sin(v)` globally.

For `x*t`: No candidate has an explicit `x*t` term, and `x*cos(c*t)` cannot produce `x*t`.

Since the GT fundamentally requires:
1. A `sin(v)` term (transcendental in v), and
2. An `x*t` term (linear in both x and t),

and no candidate can produce either of these exactly, no candidate can match the GT.

Let me double-check: could I be misreading the GT? The GT is:
`-beta*sin(v) - omega0**c0*(gamma*t + c1)*x - omega0**c2*x**c3`

With the given values, this is indeed what I computed. The `sin(v)` is essential and cannot be replicated by polynomial terms in `v`. The `x*t` cross-term also cannot be produced by any of the candidate structures.

Even if we considered approximate matching, the task asks for mathematical equivalence, which requires exact matching for all values of x, v, and t.

Expanding: `-2.5126990598325*x**3 - 2.5126990598325*x - 0.2316178862*x*t - 0.774919680656294*sin(v)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `x` (constant coefficient)
2. `x**3` (constant coefficient)
3. `x*t` (linear in both x and t)
4. `sin(v)` (sine function of v)

Now, the key issue: **sin(v)** is a transcendental function. The candidates use polynomial approximations of v (like `v`, `v**3`, `v**5`, etc.) or other combinations. The Taylor series of sin(v) = v - v³/6 + v⁵/120 - ..., which is an infinite series. No finite polynomial in v can exactly equal sin(v).

Also, the GT has `x*t` as a term. Many candidates have `x*cos(c*t)` instead. For `x*cos(c*t)` to equal `x*t` (a linear function of t), we'd need `cos(c*t) = t` which is impossible for all t.

Wait - let me reconsider. The GT has both `x` and `x*t`. Could `x*cos(c*t)` approximate these? No - cos is periodic/bounded while t is unbounded. But if c5=0, then cos(c5*t) = cos(0) = 1, making `c4*x*cos(c5*t) = c4*x`, which is just another x term. Then we'd still need an `x*t` term somewhere.

So for a candidate to match GT, it needs:
1. An `x*t` term (or equivalent)
2. A `sin(v)` term (or equivalent)
3. `x` and `x**3` terms

**None of the candidates have an explicit `x*t` term.** They have `x*cos(c*t)` which cannot produce `x*t`. Setting the cos coefficient's argument to 0 just gives another `x` term.

**None of the candidates have `sin(v)`.** They use polynomial terms in v (v, v³, v⁵, etc.) or `v*cos(c*t)`, none of which can exactly equal sin(v).

Since sin(v) cannot be represented as a finite polynomial in v (by linear independence of basis functions / transcendence), and x*t cannot be represented by x*cos(c*t), **no candidate can match the GT**.

Let me verify each candidate systematically - they all share the same fundamental issues:
- Missing `sin(v)` (replaced by polynomial terms in v)
- Missing `x*t` (replaced by `x*cos(c*t)` or similar)

For all 50 candidates, these two structural mismatches make exact equivalence impossible.
